<p>The <b>2013 UEFA Champions League Final</b> was the final match of the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2012–13 UEFA Champions League">2012–13 UEFA Champions League</a>, the 58th season of Europe's premier club <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> tournament organised by <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a>, and the 21st season since it was renamed from the European Champion Clubs' Cup to the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a>.</p>
<p>The match took place on Saturday, 25 May 2013, at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, England, between German <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga" title="Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a> clubs <a href="/wiki/Borussia_Dortmund" title="Borussia Dortmund">Borussia Dortmund</a> and <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">Bayern Munich</a>. In the first all-German Champions League final, Bayern won the match 2–1 with goals from <a href="/wiki/Mario_Mand%C5%BEuki%C4%87" title="Mario Mandžukić">Mario Mandžukić</a> and man of the match <a href="/wiki/Arjen_Robben" title="Arjen Robben">Arjen Robben</a> coming either side of an <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0lkay_G%C3%BCndo%C4%9Fan" title="İlkay Gündoğan">İlkay Gündoğan</a> penalty for Dortmund.</p>
<p>One week later, Bayern won the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_DFB-Pokal" title="2012–13 DFB-Pokal">2013 DFB-Pokal</a> and, having already won the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Bundesliga" title="2012–13 Bundesliga">2013 Bundesliga</a>, completed the <a href="/wiki/Treble_(association_football)" title="Treble (association football)">Continental Treble</a>. As a result of their Champions League win, Bayern qualified to play against <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a>, the winners of the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_UEFA_Europa_League" title="2012–13 UEFA Europa League">2012–13 UEFA Europa League</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/2013_UEFA_Super_Cup" title="2013 UEFA Super Cup">2013 UEFA Super Cup</a>, and also earned the right to enter the semi-finals of the <a href="/wiki/2013_FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="2013 FIFA Club World Cup">2013 FIFA Club World Cup</a> as the <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a> representative. They would eventually go on to win both competitions.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Venue">Venue</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_UEFA_Champions_League_Final&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Venue">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wembley_Stadium,_illuminated.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="428" data-file-width="640" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Wembley_Stadium%2C_illuminated.jpg/220px-Wembley_Stadium%2C_illuminated.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Wembley_Stadium%2C_illuminated.jpg/330px-Wembley_Stadium%2C_illuminated.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Wembley_Stadium%2C_illuminated.jpg/440px-Wembley_Stadium%2C_illuminated.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wembley_Stadium,_illuminated.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a> has hosted the European Cup final seven times, including twice in the past three seasons.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Wembley Stadium, England's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_stadium" title="National stadium">national stadium</a> and home of the <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England national football team</a>, was announced as the venue of the 2013 final on 16 June 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> Having hosted the <a href="/wiki/2011_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2011 UEFA Champions League Final">2011 final</a>, Wembley made history for being the first stadium in the tournament's history to host the final twice in three years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> Discussing the short time between the two finals, <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a> President <a href="/wiki/Michel_Platini" title="Michel Platini">Michel Platini</a> explained that the final would be in celebration of 150 years of the <a href="/wiki/The_Football_Association" title="The Football Association">Football Association</a>'s existence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> It was the seventh occasion that Wembley hosted the final after hosting the <a href="/wiki/1963_European_Cup_Final" title="1963 European Cup Final">1963</a>, <a href="/wiki/1968_European_Cup_Final" title="1968 European Cup Final">1968</a>, <a href="/wiki/1971_European_Cup_Final" title="1971 European Cup Final">1971</a>, <a href="/wiki/1978_European_Cup_Final" title="1978 European Cup Final">1978</a>, <a href="/wiki/1992_European_Cup_Final" title="1992 European Cup Final">1992</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2011_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2011 UEFA Champions League Final">2011</a> finals of Europe's premier club competition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_(1923)" title="Wembley Stadium (1923)">original Wembley Stadium</a> hosted five European Cup finals. The <a href="/wiki/1968_European_Cup_Final" title="1968 European Cup Final">1968</a> and <a href="/wiki/1978_European_Cup_Final" title="1978 European Cup Final">1978</a> finals were both won by English sides: <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> beat <a href="/wiki/S.L._Benfica" title="S.L. Benfica">Benfica</a> 4–1 in 1968 and <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> defeated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Club_Brugge_K.V." title="Club Brugge K.V.">Club Brugge</a> 1–0 in 1978. Benfica also lost in the <a href="/wiki/1963_European_Cup_Final" title="1963 European Cup Final">1963 final</a>, beaten 2–1 by <a href="/wiki/A.C._Milan" title="A.C. Milan">Milan</a>, while <a href="/wiki/AFC_Ajax" title="AFC Ajax">Ajax</a> won the first of three consecutive European Cups at Wembley in <a href="/wiki/1971_European_Cup_Final" title="1971 European Cup Final">1971</a>, beating <a href="/wiki/Panathinaikos_F.C." title="Panathinaikos F.C.">Panathinaikos</a> 2–0. In the <a href="/wiki/1992_European_Cup_Final" title="1992 European Cup Final">1992 final</a>, Spanish club <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">Barcelona</a> defeated Italian side <a href="/wiki/U.C._Sampdoria" title="U.C. Sampdoria">Sampdoria</a> 1–0 in the final match played as the European Cup prior to the following season's introduction of the current Champions League format.</p>
<p>First opened for the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire_Exhibition" title="British Empire Exhibition">British Empire Exhibition</a> in 1923, the stadium was originally known as the Empire Stadium. That year, it hosted its <a href="/wiki/1923_FA_Cup_Final" title="1923 FA Cup Final">first FA Cup Final</a>, when almost 200,000 spectators attempted to watch the match between <a href="/wiki/Bolton_Wanderers_F.C." title="Bolton Wanderers F.C.">Bolton Wanderers</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Ham_United_F.C." title="West Ham United F.C.">West Ham United</a>. Wembley played host to all of <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a>'s matches at the <a href="/wiki/1966_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1966 FIFA World Cup">1966 FIFA World Cup</a>, including the 4–2 victory over <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">West Germany</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1966_FIFA_World_Cup_Final" title="1966 FIFA World Cup Final">final</a>, and at <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1996" title="UEFA Euro 1996">UEFA Euro 1996</a>. The original stadium was closed in 2000 and demolished three years later, to be replaced by a 90,000-capacity arena, which opened in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> The new stadium hosted the <a href="/wiki/2011_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2011 UEFA Champions League Final">2011 UEFA Champions League Final</a>, which pitted <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">Barcelona</a> against <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> in a re-match of the final played two years previously. Barcelona claimed their fourth European title as they ran out 3–1 winners.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_UEFA_Champions_League_Final&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>This was the first time in the history of the Champions League (and European Cup) that the final was contested between two German sides. There were three previous Champions League finals between two clubs from the same country: <a href="/wiki/2000_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2000 UEFA Champions League Final">2000</a> (Spain), <a href="/wiki/2003_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2003 UEFA Champions League Final">2003</a> (Italy), and <a href="/wiki/2008_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2008 UEFA Champions League Final">2008</a> (England).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>It was Bayern Munich's 10th European Cup/Champions League final, third all-time behind <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C.F." title="Real Madrid C.F.">Real Madrid</a> (12) and <a href="/wiki/A.C._Milan" title="A.C. Milan">Milan</a> (11). They won four of those finals: in <a href="/wiki/1974_European_Cup_Final" title="1974 European Cup Final">1974</a>, <a href="/wiki/1975_European_Cup_Final" title="1975 European Cup Final">1975</a>, <a href="/wiki/1976_European_Cup_Final" title="1976 European Cup Final">1976</a>, and most recently in <a href="/wiki/2001_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2001 UEFA Champions League Final">2001</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> The 2013 final was Bayern's third final in four years; they lost in both <a href="/wiki/2010_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2010 UEFA Champions League Final">2010</a> and <a href="/wiki/2012_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2012 UEFA Champions League Final">2012</a> (as the first team since 1984 to reach the Final held in their home stadium), adding to previous final losses in <a href="/wiki/1982_European_Cup_Final" title="1982 European Cup Final">1982</a>, <a href="/wiki/1987_European_Cup_Final" title="1987 European Cup Final">1987</a>, and <a href="/wiki/1999_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="1999 UEFA Champions League Final">1999</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>For Dortmund, this was their second Champions League final, with them winning their first title in <a href="/wiki/1997_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="1997 UEFA Champions League Final">1997</a>. The next season as defending champions, they defeated Bayern in their only previous meetings in European competitions, winning 1–0 on aggregate in the <a href="/wiki/1997%E2%80%9398_UEFA_Champions_League" title="1997–98 UEFA Champions League">1997–98 UEFA Champions League</a> quarter-finals, before being eliminated 2–0 on aggregate in the semi-finals by Real Madrid, managed by <a href="/wiki/Jupp_Heynckes" title="Jupp Heynckes">Jupp Heynckes</a>, who took over as Bayern coach in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2003, Bayern provided a €2 million loan without collateral to the nearly bankrupt Dortmund which has since been repaid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Domestically there has been a heated rivalry between Bayern and Dortmund in recent years. In 2011–12, Dortmund won the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Bundesliga" title="2011–12 Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2012_DFB-Pokal_Final" title="2012 DFB-Pokal Final">DFB Pokal</a> with Bayern finishing runners-up in both competitions. In 2012–13, Bayern bested Dortmund for both trophies, as well as the <a href="/wiki/2012_DFL-Supercup" title="2012 DFL-Supercup">DFL-Supercup</a>. Just before Dortmund's Champions League semi-final, it was announced that one of their homegrown stars, <a href="/wiki/Mario_G%C3%B6tze" title="Mario Götze">Mario Götze</a>, would make a €37 million transfer to Bayern for the upcoming 2013–14 season,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> a move that some felt would have put more distance between wealthy Bayern and the rest of the Bundesliga.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> The final 2012–13 Bundesliga game between the two clubs was a 1–1 draw marked by acrimony as Bayern's <a href="/wiki/Rafinha_(footballer,_born_1985)" title="Rafinha (footballer, born 1985)">Rafinha</a> was sent off for elbowing Dortmund's Jakub Blaszczykowski, sparking an argument on the touchline between Dortmund coach Jürgen Klopp and Bayern sporting director Matthias Sammer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> The press has used terms like 'power shift' and 'changing of the guard' after Dortmund and Bayern eliminated Spanish giants Real Madrid and Barcelona, respectively, in the Champions League semi-finals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Road_to_the_final">Road to the final</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_UEFA_Champions_League_Final&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Road to the final">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">For more details on this topic, see <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2012–13 UEFA Champions League">2012–13 UEFA Champions League</a>.</div>
<p><i>Note: In all results below, the score of the finalist is given first.</i></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-match">Pre-match</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_UEFA_Champions_League_Final&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Pre-match">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BVB-Fans_in_Wembley.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1836" data-file-width="3264" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/BVB-Fans_in_Wembley.jpg/220px-BVB-Fans_in_Wembley.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/BVB-Fans_in_Wembley.jpg/330px-BVB-Fans_in_Wembley.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/BVB-Fans_in_Wembley.jpg/440px-BVB-Fans_in_Wembley.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BVB-Fans_in_Wembley.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Borussia Dortmund fans in Wembley before kick-off</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ambassador">Ambassador</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_UEFA_Champions_League_Final&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Ambassador">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The two-time Champions League winner and ex-England international <a href="/wiki/Steve_McManaman" title="Steve McManaman">Steve McManaman</a> was appointed as the official ambassador for the final.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Opening_ceremony">Opening ceremony</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_UEFA_Champions_League_Final&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Opening ceremony">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Opening_ceremony" title="Opening ceremony">opening ceremony</a> was directed by <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Spacey" title="Kevin Spacey">Kevin Spacey</a>'s executive assistant and <a href="/wiki/The_Prince%27s_Trust" title="The Prince's Trust">The Prince's Trust</a> ambassador Hamish Jenkinson and his business partner Jonny Grant, who had previously directed the 2011 opening ceremony, also at Wembley. The ceremony, also titled "Battle of Kings", was produced by Films United. It was directed and produced by <a href="/wiki/Grigorij_Richters" title="Grigorij Richters">Grigorij Richters</a> and his producing partner Alex Souabni. Both were the former filmmakers-in-residence of <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Spacey" title="Kevin Spacey">Kevin Spacey</a> and Jenkinson at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Old_Vic_Theatre" title="The Old Vic Theatre">The Old Vic Theatre</a> in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>. The film focused around the story of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Activist" title="Activist">activist</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fundraiser" title="Fundraiser">fundraiser</a> <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Sutton" title="Stephen Sutton">Stephen Sutton</a>, who was part of the group of performers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Match_ball">Match ball</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_UEFA_Champions_League_Final&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Match ball">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The match ball for the final was the Adidas Finale Wembley, which featured the same "Starball" panel configuration as the last three finals. The ball was predominantly white, with each star in blue with yellow patterning and a purple border. Six of the 12 stars featured designs recalling the six previous times that the European Cup final had been held at Wembley Stadium. The ball was unveiled on 30 January 2013 and was used for all knockout stage matches in the 2012–13 competition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ticketing">Ticketing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_UEFA_Champions_League_Final&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Ticketing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The international ticket sales phase for the general public ran from 11 February to 15 March 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Tickets were available in four price categories: <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">£</a>330, £230, £140, and £60. Due to the high demand for tickets, allocation was determined by a lottery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>The two finalist clubs were allocated 25,000 tickets each. Borussia Dortmund received 502,567 requests for tickets,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-borussiatickets_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-borussiatickets-31">[31]</a></sup> while there were approximately 250,000 orders for tickets from members of Bayern Munich.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bayerntickets_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-bayerntickets-32">[32]</a></sup> Both clubs used draws as a means of awarding tickets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-borussiatickets_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-borussiatickets-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bayerntickets_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-bayerntickets-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Related_events">Related events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_UEFA_Champions_League_Final&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Related events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As is the annual custom, the UEFA Champions League and UEFA Women's Champions League trophies were presented to the host city at a special ceremony at <a href="/wiki/Banqueting_House,_Whitehall" title="Banqueting House, Whitehall">Banqueting House, Whitehall</a>, on 19 April 2013. Receiving the trophies from UEFA President <a href="/wiki/Michel_Platini" title="Michel Platini">Michel Platini</a> were the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minister_for_Sport_and_the_Olympics" title="Minister for Sport and the Olympics">Minister for Sport and the Olympics</a> <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Robertson_(politician)" title="Hugh Robertson (politician)">Hugh Robertson</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_London" title="Mayor of London">Mayor of London</a>'s commissioner for sport, <a href="/wiki/Kate_Hoey" title="Kate Hoey">Kate Hoey</a>. Representing the previous season's competition winners were <a href="/wiki/John_Terry" title="John Terry">John Terry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Lampard" title="Frank Lampard">Frank Lampard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Petr_%C4%8Cech" title="Petr Čech">Petr Čech</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Torres" title="Fernando Torres">Fernando Torres</a> and <a href="/wiki/Branislav_Ivanovi%C4%87" title="Branislav Ivanović">Branislav Ivanović</a> of <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lotta_Schelin" title="Lotta Schelin">Lotta Schelin</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olympique_Lyonnais_(Ladies)" title="Olympique Lyonnais (Ladies)">Lyon</a> ladies' team. Also in attendance were final ambassadors <a href="/wiki/Graeme_Le_Saux" title="Graeme Le Saux">Graeme Le Saux</a> and <a href="/wiki/Faye_White" title="Faye White">Faye White</a>, who had escorted the trophies from <a href="/wiki/Stamford_Bridge_(stadium)" title="Stamford Bridge (stadium)">Stamford Bridge</a> to Banqueting House via London's public transport system, and <a href="/wiki/David_Bernstein_(executive)" title="David Bernstein (executive)">David Bernstein</a>, the chairman of <a href="/wiki/The_Football_Association" title="The Football Association">The Football Association</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>The UEFA Champions Festival was held at the International Quarter, <a href="/wiki/Stratford_City" title="Stratford City">Stratford City</a>, next to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olympic_Park,_London" title="Olympic Park, London">Queen Elizabeth Olympic Park</a>, from 23 to 26 May 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/2013_UEFA_Women%27s_Champions_League_Final" title="2013 UEFA Women's Champions League Final">2013 UEFA Women's Champions League Final</a> was held at <a href="/wiki/Stamford_Bridge_(stadium)" title="Stamford Bridge (stadium)">Stamford Bridge</a> on 23 May 2013 between <a href="/wiki/VfL_Wolfsburg_(women)" title="VfL Wolfsburg (women)">Wolfsburg</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olympique_Lyonnais_(ladies)" title="Olympique Lyonnais (ladies)">Lyon</a>. Wolfsburg won the game, with <a href="/wiki/Martina_M%C3%BCller_(footballer)" title="Martina Müller (footballer)">Martina Müller</a> scoring the only goal. This ensured that for the first time ever the same nation won both the men's and women's European club titles in the same year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Match">Match</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_UEFA_Champions_League_Final&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Match">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Team_news">Team news</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_UEFA_Champions_League_Final&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Team news">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Borussia Dortmund's <a href="/wiki/Mario_G%C3%B6tze" title="Mario Götze">Mario Götze</a>, who would join Bayern Munich in the summer, missed the match with a hamstring injury that had kept him out since the semi-final second leg against Real Madrid. Right-back <a href="/wiki/%C5%81ukasz_Piszczek" title="Łukasz Piszczek">Łukasz Piszczek</a> did play, however, despite being due for hip surgery, while centre-back <a href="/wiki/Mats_Hummels" title="Mats Hummels">Mats Hummels</a> recovered from a sprained ankle in time to play.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Bayern Munich were without defender <a href="/wiki/Holger_Badstuber" title="Holger Badstuber">Holger Badstuber</a>, who was expected to be out for 10 months with a knee injury,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Toni_Kroos" title="Toni Kroos">Toni Kroos</a>, who had yet to recover from an injury sustained in the quarter-final.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Summary">Summary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_UEFA_Champions_League_Final&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Summary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Dortmund were the dominant team in the first half-hour of the match, with intense pressing towards Bayern. Neuer made five important saves in the first 35 minutes, including two off shots from Lewandowski and one from Reus. Bayern later took the initiative, and scored the first goal in the 60th minute, when Mandžukić finished left footed the combination of passes by Robben and Ribéry, the ball going past Schmelzer on the goal line from three yards out.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Shortly after, Dante raised his foot in the penalty area and caught Reus in the stomach; Gündoğan scored the resulting penalty shooting low into the right corner and sending Neuer the wrong way. Robben scored the winning goal with a weak low shot pushing the ball past the onrushing Weidenfeller with his left foot from eight yards out, after a back-heeled pass from Ribéry with a minute left in normal time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Details">Details</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_UEFA_Champions_League_Final&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Details">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p><b>Match rules</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-regulations_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-regulations-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>90 minutes.</li>
<li>30 minutes of <a href="/wiki/Overtime_(sports)#Association_football" title="Overtime (sports)">extra time</a> if necessary.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Penalty_shoot-out_(association_football)" title="Penalty shoot-out (association football)">Penalty shoot-out</a> if scores still level.</li>
<li>Seven named substitutes.</li>
<li>Maximum of three substitutions.</li>
</ul>
</td>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-match_reactions">Post-match reactions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_UEFA_Champions_League_Final&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Post-match reactions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Borussia Dortmund's manager Jürgen Klopp commented that the long season caught up with Dortmund. "It was late in the game and from the 75th minute it was very hard for us after a tough season, but we deserved to be in the final and we showed that tonight" he said.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> Borussia Dortmund defender Mats Hummels said the game was really close and very disappointing, and that they were the better team in the first 25 minutes but missed the goal that was needed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> Bayern Munich's manager Jupp Heynckes said that "We have achieved something unique".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
